## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |

| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# End-to-End: How Kubernetes Creates a Deployment

## Your Task

You are onboarding to the Kubernetes project. A senior engineer has asked you to produce
a technical explanation of how a Kubernetes Deployment gets created — tracing the full
request flow from a client application through the API server and into persistent storage.

**Your question**: Explain how a Kubernetes client application creates a Deployment from
start to finish. Your explanation must trace through all three layers:

1. **Client library** — What type/function in `kubernetes-client-go` sends the HTTP request?
2. **API server** — What function in `kubernetes/kubernetes` receives and validates the create request?
3. **Storage** — What function in `etcd-io/etcd` persists the Deployment to the key-value store?

For each step, cite the specific repository, file path, and function/type name.

## Context

You are working in a Kubernetes ecosystem with the following repos:

- `kubernetes/kubernetes` (the core orchestrator)
- `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` (go-client-library)
- `sg-evals/kubernetes-api` (api-type-definitions)
- `etcd-io/etcd` (distributed-kv-store)

This question is specifically designed to benefit from cross-repo synthesis. Use your
search tools to trace the full path across repositories.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings:

```json
{
  "chain": [
    {
      "repo": "sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go",
      "path": "relative/path/to/file.go",
      "symbol": "FunctionOrTypeName",
      "description": "What this step does in the flow"
    }
  ],
  "text": "Comprehensive narrative explaining the end-to-end flow, citing specific files and functions from each repo."
}
```

**Important**: Use exact repo identifiers as they appear in Sourcegraph. The oracle expects `repo` values of `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` (client layer), `kubernetes/kubernetes` (API server layer), and `etcd-io/etcd` (storage layer). The `repo` field must match these exactly.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`). Strip this prefix in your answer — use `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, NOT `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`.

The `chain` should contain at least 3 steps representing the 3 layers described above.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **Flow coverage**: Does the chain include key steps from all 3 layers (client → server → storage)?
- **Technical accuracy**: Are the cited file paths and function names correct?
- **Provenance**: Does your narrative reference all three repositories?
- **Synthesis quality** (supplementary): Does the explanation connect the layers clearly?

I've successfully created a comprehensive technical explanation of how a Kubernetes Deployment gets created, tracing the full request flow across all three layers.

## Summary

The answer is now saved at `/workspace/answer.json` and includes:

### **The Three Layers:**

1. **Client Library (sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go)**
   - `kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/deployment.go:DeploymentInterface.Create`
   - Sends HTTP POST request through RESTClient

2. **API Server (kubernetes/kubernetes)**
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go:createHandler`
   - Receives and validates the request
   - `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go:REST.Create`
   - Applies Deployment-specific strategies and validation
   - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go:store.Create`
   - Serializes and prepares for persistence

3. **Storage/etcd (etcd-io-etcd)**
   - `server/mvcc/kv.go:WriteView.Put`
   - Key-value store interface for writes
   - `server/mvcc/kvstore.go:store`
   - MVCC implementation that manages versions and transactions
   - Persists to BoltDB backend

The explanation traces how the Deployment object flows from client serialization → HTTP transmission → API server validation → storage encoding → etcd MVCC versioning → persistent storage, with each layer adding validation, transformation, and durability guarantees.

An application calls the `Create()` method on a `DeploymentInterface` object (defined in `kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/deployment.go`). This interface is implemented by the `deployments` struct, which wraps `gentype.ClientWithListAndApply`. The Create method constructs an HTTP POST request containing the serialized Deployment manifest and sends it to the API server's REST endpoint.\\n\\n**API SERVER LAYER (kubernetes-kubernetes):**\\nThe HTTP POST request arrives at the Kubernetes API server, where it is routed to the `createHandler` function in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`. This handler:\\n1. Extracts the namespace and object name from the request\\n2. Deserializes the request body into a Deployment object\\n3. Performs admission control checks\\n4. Calls the `Create()` method on a `rest.Creater` implementation\\n\\nFor Deployments, the Creater is the `REST` struct defined in `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go`. The etcd3 backend interfaces with the MVCC (Multi-Version Concurrency Control) engine defined in `server/mvcc/kvstore.go`. A write transaction is created (implementing the `TxnWrite` interface from `server/mvcc/kv.go`), and the serialized Deployment is written to the key-value store via the `Put()` method defined in the `WriteView` interface. \\n\\nThe `Put()` method in `server/mvcc/kvstore.go` performs the actual write operation, allocating a new revision number, updating the in-memory index, and persisting the key-value pair to the underlying BoltDB backend. The transaction is then committed, making the Deployment object durable and visible to all future read operations.\\n\\n**Summary:**\\nThe complete flow is: client application \u2192 kubernetes-client-go REST Client \u2192 API server HTTP handler \u2192 DeploymentInterface.Create() \u2192 REST storage Create() \u2192 etcd3 store.Create() \u2192 etcd MVCC store Put() \u2192 persistent storage (BoltDB). Each layer adds validation, transformation, and durability guarantees, ensuring that the Deployment specification is accurately stored and can be retrieved by controllers and other clients.\"\n}\n",
